The dislocation of the hand
The joint of the hand dislocates, and its return is light, more than the other joints. However, it is necessary to bring it back to its place immediately, in the same hour that it is dislocated, so that the limb becomes swollen or that an abscess comes hot.
And the bringing back is that you put the sick hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and he places it equal, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes it until it returns.
However, it is necessary that you look to see if it is well in its place; then put the sick person's back of his hand on a table at extension and return. And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then the patient puts the back of their hand on the table, and the healer places their hand above the appearance of the joint.
If it returns now, it is well. If not, apply poultices of soothing plasters, and let him leave so as not to restart.
And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in its place after several days, the joint remains twisted.
and does not harm the patient further than that while his hand is weakened and cannot grasp anything at all. Therefore, know that the nerve is severed, or the artery.
If there is no other remedy except to constrict with a cautery according to the case, and perhaps it is worth nothing else.
And when the hand is in place, put on the splint that we have said, then restrain it and leave it for 5 days, then untie it and leave it so.
And if he cannot move it well, and there is no wound, then moisten it with hot water, and rub it until it is sound.
of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
At no time are the bones of the hand dislocated on each side, at no time on the back of the palm or on the belly;
Therefore, they are the bones, and push the dislocation into your pouches until it returns, then support the head of the bone, and lean it towards the part where it is dislocated;
and leave it for two days, and then put it even on that day.
and of the knot we have said, and untie it each day, and let it move, and tie the knot again.
And do this often, until it is tight, and just as well if it is dislocated in the palm of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed.
And just as well if it is dislocated from elsewhere.
of the dislocation of the spine of the back
When the spine of the back or the neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, if there is no cure, because death hastens the patient.
And the signs are that the joints jump out without volition, and cannot be held in place, and many times are softened any limb, or the two hips or the two arms or one.
And many times it moves the joint at four parts.
The one that moves at the back is called "gilbositez":
The cure of this is that you reward if the gilbositez came from childhood. if there is no cure nor healing of all.
And those that come from falling or blows or similar things, said the old ways of cure with great words, in which there is not much profit at all.
but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
I say that in the swelling that comes to the breast before, there is nothing nor healing;
and also that which comes directly in the two sides, and one cannot cure except for that properly which comes to the back, as I say;
and it is that the patient be stretched on his face in a level place, and have a strain below him so that he does not bleed.
then put the tinder in the head into the earth forming, and the other at the feet, and tie a linen below the hips of the patient, and the other at the waist, knees, and ankles.
and the minister knows the links, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two bones.
and they should be well closed, the bones as we have said, and the mire puts his palms on the spine forming, until it returns.
And if it does not return by this cure, then take a board of III arms long, and place it under the loin, and the patient be on his side, and push the head of the board under the loin, then put the middle of the board on the spine; and put the mire his feet on the other head of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place;
and if you see, then do it with the turning crank that turns by hand. And is that you put two bones at the head of the sick person of one arm of great length, and towards the feet two others, and between each bone, above and below, a palm's width of length;
and have in each twig a hole pierced, or the turn (of the fire) is corrected, and be the twigs firmly in earth, so that they do not move.
and between each two twigs have one turning twig, so that the line turns, and have in each turning two small twigs of an arm's length, to turn the fire.
and then tie the line which is among the ashes to the fire towards the head, and the other line towards the feet to the other fire, and each of the ministers turns his fire all along the line, and the master puts the spine straight as we have said.
And when it is straightened, place on top a drying plaster with abundance of egg white, and then the bandages, and then the splint of a tablet of three fingers' length, that covers the location of the gibbosity and the part of the healthy spine, then bind it with a line as we have said, and use the patient to subtle nourishment, until he is healed;
And if any thing comes at the end of health, it is fitting to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the method that we have said before; And sometimes one administers a piece of lead, and sometimes it comes to the appearance in the lower vertebra of the back, and one thinks that it is dislocation; and it is the bone which opens, therefore one should not have presumption there: for it might bring death by chance.
Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder come out only with dislocations, and do not come out like the other joints;
and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to IV parts: inward and outward, and forward and backward;
and more inward then, and less dislocated forward and backward.
And the knowledge of its dislocation within it is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens more the diseased knee than the healthy one, and the diseased one cannot double his knee at the fire. And it is the limb which is beneath swollen with a hot abscess, because of that the head of the hip comes near.
And the sign of him to whom it comes on the outward side, is that this accident is contrary to those before.
And the signs of him who has it in front, is that his leg is well according to its fulfillment; However, he does not double his knee without pain, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot before, and retains his urine, and inflates the groin, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.
And the sign of him to whom it happens behind, is that he cannot spread his knee or double it, and his leg is more twisted than the other, and his anger is softened, and his hip is at the place below the ribs.
The returning of this kind of dislocation is that you reward if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its disposition, there is no cure; and he must have no presumption.
And in this one whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of these four manners of dislocation, so hasten that you return the joint, and the length inside and outside, and the movement to right and left. perhaps it will return, and there is no need for other care.
And if it does not return in this manner, then it is necessary that you apply the minister strongly, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or on the ligament that lies above the knee; and another minister extends his hand above in such a manner that he pushes his hands below his shoulders, then tightly grips with a forceful pull on the hip. and another holds the head of the ligament
and extend upward and downward all at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains suspended.
This manner of extension is common to four similar things, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
If this is not so, then it is necessary to take care of its appearance.
When the dislocation is at the hip, then it is necessary that you support the patient on his healthy side, then place the linen on the root of the thigh, and the one that is below the groin, then extend the linen upwards towards the groin, and towards the thigh;
then grasp with other ministers his arms, and embrace the large root of the diseased thigh, and extend it outwardly formed: if it will return to its place now;
and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
And if you cannot tighten it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong linen strip above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the diseased leg be extended two times more than the other;
Then he must be hung by the head of a pole, and on the ground two arms' length.
Then command to the minister that he embrace the head of the hip, and let other ministers stand with the patient, who firmly embrace the hip, for the joint returns now quickly.
And when the dislocation is at the back, let the patient lie down, as we have said in the one who has gibbosity, and restrain the limb on the leg properly, and on the foot also.
Then put two sticks, one at the head and one at the foot, then place a stick between the hips of the patient to help form it. And have bundles of damp cloths around it so that it doesn't burn the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and the minister puts his hand on the dislocation evenly.
If it returns, it is good.
If this is not so, put him on a table,  and press him as we have said in the glossary, and lay the patient on his healthy side.
And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the injured leg as much as possible, and according to what I have said. and puts the hands his pain on the angry sick, then presses with the other hand, and the end down toward the knee.
And if the dislocation is at the back, it is not necessary to extend the sick person down, nor raise up on the ground, but rather that he be as though the hip was dislocated at the back, as we have said about lying on the two hips. and be on his face, and the band extended as we have said before, and one must press upon the joint to the table. and it will be at point when the sick person extends his legs, and they will be equal. then adjust the thighs, and put the splint, and the band of a bandage, so that the hip does not move. and rest for three days or four, then undo it, and put the splint on top.
and if you see that they are even, hold them, as before, and let it be three days;
then untie it, and allow it to move freely, until the limb is fortified.
of the dislocation of the knee
The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind;
and does not dislocate in front.
And the sign is that you command the patient to bend his leg at his hip, and if he cannot bring it to his hip, know that it is dislocated;
and the restoration of all of them is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his thigh, and put his foot on your feet;
then take his knee in your palms, and draw it between your two hands, then bend the two bones that form the knee. And some other ministers extend their foot, so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he feels his leg at his hip lightly.
And put the plaster on top, and make him raise his leg to his hip, and let them be bound together for three or four days, then untie it.
And do not let the patient work at all to go, until the limbs are strengthened.
And if the limb is not in place, administer a strong stretching, as we have said in the cure of the hip, until it is healed.
of the dislocation of the heel
The heels are sometimes dislocated and sometimes completely dislocated, inside and outside.
And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and tender in front of where it was dislocated:
The return should be gentle, and one must extend it gently with his hands when he is just numbed.
And when it is dislocated completely, then you must have the patient sit upright, and hold him down by one minister by the leg, above the ankle;
Then treat the foot with your right hand, then with your left twice, then extend it upwards, and push the foot up nicely.
and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot;
If it returns, that's good;
if not, begin the work again, for it will return.
and if it cannot return this way, then make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and stick a  rail firmly into the ground between their hips, and tie cloths around it so that it doesn't move the patient.
then hold the hips with ministers, and other ministers extend the foot to their hands or to the rail so that they tie it above the ankle. then extend each minister equally, and the rail should be placed between the hips of the patient to hold them down while being extended.
Then put the mire equal the dislocation with his hands, and others ministers hold the sound leg at the groin, and the dislocation will return easily.
And when it is pointed, put the plaster and stoppings on top, and the strain forms, and tie the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the bonds are not too tight.
Then let him leave it for two or three days, and if the bonds soften, tighten them again.
Then unbind on the third day or the fourth, and forbid the patient from walking for four days. And if he goes before that term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
And if an abscess comes to it then you must soothe it as we have said elsewhere until it is healed.
of two When the hips are dislocated, it is necessary to extend them well without effort, and it is a light thing.
And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back or foot, then it behooves you to make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a table quite straight, and put your foot upon what separates the joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it comes back.
And when it is aligned and there is nothing separating it, then put under the sole of the foot a board two hands wide, then restrain it firmly, and leave it for three days, then unbind it. And make him rest until he is healed.
Of wounds and dislocations together
When a wound comes with the dislocation, and it is wanted to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies:
if you are not modest in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and patient, nor too bold;
and use at the beginning of things soothing poultices hot, and leave the patient in God's hands, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope in it, then set the limb now to its place, so that the abscess may come to a head there;
and when the limb is in place, then administer soothing poultices hot, and treat the wound as it is necessary, with dried dressings;
and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are dislocated, set them, and do what we have said in simple ailments;
And guard yourself from entering into the way of fear, according to what I have said, for it brings you misfortune according to your Creator, and for the safety of your arm and your body.
